# DnD Rules Coverage And Experience TODO

> Baseline date: 2026-05-27
> Scope: AI DnD 5e playable Alpha toward an AI-driven CRPG experience.
> Multiplayer target: about 50 concurrent online users on one server, across isolated rooms; each multiplayer game room remains capped around 4 players.

This document is the long-running TODO for two tracks:

- DnD 5e rule coverage: keep math, dice, resources, and state transitions in the backend rule engine.
- Experience quality: make single-player and 4-player multiplayer sessions feel stable, readable, and game-like under real use.

The percentages below are working estimates, not product promises. Update them when a feature is implemented and verified with tests or a manual playthrough.

## Current Snapshot

| Area | Current Estimate | Notes |
| --- | ---: | --- |
| Playable single-player experience | 75-80% | Core adventure, DM response, skill checks, combat entry, and character state are usable. |
| 4-player multiplayer game experience | 65-70% | Room, membership, turn ownership, WS updates, and combat sync exist; long-session recovery still needs pressure. |
| 50 online users across rooms | 80-85% | 50-user/13-room WS smoke has repeated local coverage, including 2026-05-31 browser hold verification and cleanup-log regression after a WS presence race fix; still needs regular CI repetition and production-like telemetry. |
| Core playable DnD rules | 60-70% | Common combat math, turns, reactions, death saves, conditions, key spells, spell action economy, and first monster traits are present. |
| Full DnD 5e coverage | 35-45% | Long tail remains: full spell behavior, subclasses, advanced monster traits, exploration procedures, and edge cases. |
| BG-style CRPG experience | 35-45% | The system has the right skeleton; encounter design, UI polish, tactical depth, and persistence need much more work. |

## Status Legend

| Mark | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `[x]` | Implemented and covered by tests or a verified playthrough. |
| `[~]` | Partially implemented or implemented but not fully verified. |
| `[ ]` | Not implemented, shallow, or not trusted yet. |

Priority:

- P0: needed for stable playable sessions.
- P1: needed for a satisfying DnD-feeling Alpha.
- P2: needed for deep 5e coverage or CRPG depth.

2026-06-12 Spell preparation frontend follow-up: `PrepareSpellsModal` now loads `/characters/options` and uses `spell_preparation_type` plus the normalized class key to choose the correct preparation source. Prepared casters choose from `class_spells`, spellbook casters stay limited to known spellbook entries, known-spell casters render as locked instead of offering a daily subset, and the displayed preparation limit mirrors the half-caster rule for Paladin-style prepared casters. Adventure's preparation entry now recognizes explicit `preparation_type` values and Paladin in addition to Wizard/Cleric/Druid. Covered by `npm run test -- src\components\adventure\__tests__\PrepareSpellsModal.test.jsx src\hooks\__tests__\useAdventureUiState.test.js` (`2 files / 7 passed`), `npm run build`, and backend contract coverage `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_spell_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py::test_prepared_caster_can_prepare_spells_from_class_list -q` (`9 passed`).

2026-06-12 Level-up spell learning backend follow-up: `POST /characters/{character_id}/level-up` now accepts `learned_spells` and `learned_cantrips`, validates choices during the same trusted level-up transaction, persists updated `known_spells` / `cantrips`, and returns `level_up_details.learned_spells`, `learned_cantrips`, and `preparation_type`. The first trusted rules slice lets Wizard add up to 2 leveled spellbook entries per level, known-spell casters add up to 1 leveled spell, prepared casters cannot learn leveled spells through level-up because they prepare from the class list, and cantrip learning is only allowed when the class cantrip threshold increases. Choices are checked against the class spell/cantrip lists and duplicates are rejected. OpenAPI and generated frontend API types were refreshed. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\schemas\character_requests.py backend\api\character_progression.py backend\services\character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py`, targeted backend coverage `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py -q` (`19 passed`), `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe backend\scripts\export_openapi.py`, `npm run types:api`, and `npm run build`. Remaining work is a frontend level-up spell-choice UI plus fuller pact/known-spell progression tables.

2026-06-12 Level-up spell learning frontend follow-up: CharacterSheet now loads `/characters/options`, builds a level-up spell choice plan from the character's class, current level, preparation type, known spells, and cantrips, and exposes a compact Level Up panel. Wizard/spellbook characters can pick up to two new class spells, known casters can be planned for one known spell, prepared casters do not receive leveled spell learning choices, and cantrip options appear only when the next level raises the class cantrip threshold. Confirming the panel calls `charactersApi.levelUp()` with `learned_spells` / `learned_cantrips`, then updates the sheet from the returned character and surfaces a learned-spells notice. Covered by `npm run test -- src\utils\__tests__\levelUpSpellChoices.test.js src\pages\__tests__\CharacterSheet.inventory.test.jsx` (`2 files / 7 passed`), backend regression `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py::test_level_up_adds_requested_wizard_spell_learning -q` (`14 passed`), `node --check frontend\src\utils\levelUpSpellChoices.js`, and `npm run build`. Remaining work is fuller pact/known-spell progression tables plus the broader ASI/feat/feature UI.

2026-06-12 Known-spell progression table follow-up: `SPELLS_KNOWN` now drives level-up spell-learning capacity for Bard, Ranger, Sorcerer, and Warlock instead of giving every known caster a flat one-spell choice on every level. Warlock 9->10 correctly blocks new known spells, Warlock 10->11 allows one, and Ranger 1->2 can learn two 1st-level spells while still rejecting spells above the next level's slot access. `/characters/options` now keeps the legacy `class_spells` name list and also returns `class_spell_details` with `{name, level}` so CharacterSheet can filter level-up choices before submission; Paladin/Ranger remain exposed for class spell list use, while character creation avoids adding an empty level-1 half-caster spell-choice step when no starting spell/cantrip selection is required. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\services\character_options_service.py backend\services\character_leveling_service.py backend\services\dnd_data.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_options_service.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py`, `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_options_service.py -q` (`20 passed`), `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_options_service.py -q` (`9 passed`), `node --check frontend\src\utils\levelUpSpellChoices.js`, and `npm run test -- src\utils\__tests__\levelUpSpellChoices.test.js src\utils\__tests__\characterCreate.test.js src\pages\__tests__\CharacterSheet.inventory.test.jsx` (`3 files / 17 passed`). 2026-06-12 All-class level-up playthrough first slice: service-layer and endpoint-layer parameterized checks now create every supported class from the shared `HIT_DICE` table, level each character from 1 to 2, and assert the core invariants that previously only had point coverage: `old_level/new_level`, average HP gain, `hp_current`, recalculated `derived.hp_max`, hit die, proficiency bonus, caster type, new spell-slot capacity, persisted spell slots, unchanged known spell/cantrip lists when no choices are submitted, and class-resource keys/types staying inside their level-2 defaults. The endpoint pass calls real `POST /characters/{character_id}/level-up`, refreshes the database row, and confirms persisted level, HP, spell slots, known spells, and cantrips match the response. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py::test_build_level_up_update_supports_level_one_to_two_for_all_classes -q` (`12 passed`), `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py::test_level_up_endpoint_supports_level_one_to_two_for_all_classes -q` (`12 passed`), `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_character_progression_endpoints.py backend\tests\unit\test_character_options_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_full_game_flow.py -q` (`74 passed`), `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\tests\unit\test_character_leveling_service.py backend\services\character_leveling_service.py`, and frontend guard coverage `npm run test -- src\utils\__tests__\levelUpSpellChoices.test.js src\utils\__tests__\characterCreate.test.js src\pages\__tests__\CharacterSheet.inventory.test.jsx` (`3 files / 17 passed`). Remaining work is subclass milestone playthroughs, higher-level ASI/feat/feature choices, and spell replacement/swap rules.

2026-06-12 Feature-level class-resource unlock follow-up: class-resource defaults now stop exposing several features before their 5e-like unlock levels: Rogue no longer gets `cunning_action_available` until level 2, Druid no longer gets `wild_shape_remaining` until level 2, Cleric no longer gets `channel_divinity_used` until level 2, and Paladin keeps level-1 Lay on Hands but does not get `channel_divinity_used` until level 3. Level-up still unlocks those resources at the milestone, while `_advance_class_resources()` now preserves an existing legacy resource's current remaining value when the old level did not own that resource yet, avoiding an accidental pseudo-rest for migrated saves. Martial Arts is now a narrow attack-roll action exposed from the Monk skill bar after a completed Attack action: it spends the bonus action without incrementing `attacks_made`, rejects equipped shields, consumes no weapon/ammo/thrown resources, uses proficiency plus the best STR/DEX modifier for hit, uses the level-scaling Martial Arts die plus the best STR/DEX modifier for damage, marks the pending attack as `is_martial_arts`, and carries `damage_type="bludgeoning"` through damage resolution. ### Turn Economy

| Status | Priority | Rule Area | Current State | Done Definition |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [x] | P0 | Initiative and turn order | Combat state tracks turn order/current turn. | Player, AI companion, and enemy turns advance deterministically in single and multiplayer. |
| [x] | P0 | Action tracking | Turn state tracks action, bonus action, reaction, movement. | Every combat endpoint refuses illegal extra use and reports clear reason to UI. |
| [x] | P0 | Movement budget | Movement used/max are tracked. | Move endpoint enforces speed, difficult terrain, prone stand-up cost, grapple/restrained speed, and opportunity triggers. |
| [~] | P1 | Dash/disengage/help/dodge | Several action keys and effects exist. 2026-05-30: direct `/game/combat/{session_id}/action` dash/disengage/help/dodge now share the actor-state action gate, so stunned/incapacitated actors cannot bypass turn-state rules through these basic actions; covered by `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_rules_endpoints.py`. 2026-06-04 follow-up: real headless Chrome smoke `OPPORTUNITY_SMOKE_MODE=disengage node artifacts/opportunity-attack-move-browser-smoke.mjs` clicked the live `Ķä▒ń”╗µÄźµłś` skill before moving from `5,5` to `10,5`, verified `action_used=true`, `disengaged=true`, movement used `5/6`, player HP stayed 20, enemy `reaction_used=false`, no opportunity attack dice/log appeared, and cleanup returned `0/0/0`; screenshot `artifacts/browser-opportunity-attack-disengage-move-20260604.png`. 2026-06-06 Dodge follow-up: AI attacks against a dodging target now preserve `roll_state="disadvantage"` and `disadvantage_sources=["target dodging"]`; frontend rule tags/logs localize the source as `ńø«µĀćķŚ¬ķü┐`; real browser smoke `OPPORTUNITY_SMOKE_MODE=dodge-attack-disadvantage node artifacts/run-opportunity-smoke.mjs` clicked live Dodge, ended turn, resolved the AI attack, verified visible Dodge disadvantage feedback, and cleanup returned `0/0/0` with no `8002` listener. 2026-06-06 Help follow-up: derived combat entities now carry turn-state metadata so helped allies surface `õĖŗµ¼Īµö╗Õć╗õ╝śÕŖ┐` in TargetCard/HUD before attacking; real browser smoke `OPPORTUNITY_SMOKE_MODE=help-attack-advantage node artifacts/run-opportunity-smoke.mjs` clicked live Help on Mara Quickstep, verified the visible advantage chip, then resolved Mara's `/attack-roll` with `roll_state="advantage"` and `advantage_sources=["attacker helped"]`, consuming `being_helped`; cleanup returned `0/0/0` with no `8002` listener. | All basic actions are exposed in UI, enforce action economy, and affect attacks/movement exactly once. |
| [~] | P1 | Ready action | 2026-06-04 first trusted slice: players can declare a backend-trusted ready attack from the combat skill bar, storing `turn_state.ready_action`, spending the action, and exposing the mode as `ready_attack`. Ready action 2026-06-04 movement follow-up: `ready_move` is now exposed from the attack skill mode group. Attack, Move, and Spell ready-action resolvers now return a visible `ready_action_results[0]` payload with `applied=false`, `reason="reaction_already_used"`, `reaction_already_used=true`, preserved `condition_text`, and a `ready_action_failed` turn-state snapshot; the result is also logged and included in multiplayer `entity_moved` broadcasts. Real WS smoke `ENEMY_READY_SMOKE_MODE=reaction-spent-trigger BACKEND_ORIGIN=http://127.0.0.1:8002 node artifacts\enemy-ready-action-ws-smoke.mjs` registered a real user, seeded a real multiplayer combat with an enemy ready attack whose reaction was already spent, moved `Ready Smoke Hero` from `5,5` to `6,5`, and verified `entity_moved.ready_action_results[0]` with `applied=false`, `reason="reaction_already_used"`, condition text `When Ready Smoke Hero crosses the bridge, slash.`, no attack roll, hero HP still 20, enemy `reaction_used=true`, no remaining enemy `ready_action`, and `ready_action_failed` preserved in turn state; cleanup returned browser/profile/snapshot `0/0/0`, and no `8002`, `3000`, or `3100` listener remained after shutdown. Remaining Ready Action work is deeper custom trigger matching semantics.

Ready action 2026-06-08 structured `trigger_match` follow-up: ready-action declarations now carry a trusted movement predicate alongside display-only `condition_text`. The backend normalizes and stores `trigger_match` as `any_movement`, `enters_reach`, or `leaves_reach`; `any_movement` preserves the old trigger-on-tracked-movement behavior, while `enters_reach` and `leaves_reach` use old/new Chebyshev grid distance from the readied actor to the moving target so custom trigger text no longer has to imply the rule predicate by itself. `/ready-action` accepts the field for attack/spell/move payloads, Ready Action expiry/failure/result payloads preserve it, and the combat HUD exposes a compact trigger selector (`õ╗╗µäÅń¦╗ÕŖ©`, `Ķ┐øÕģźĶ¦”ÕÅŖ`, `ń”╗Õ╝ĆĶ¦”ÕÅŖ`) that flows through Ready Attack, Ready Spell, and two-step Ready Move destination selection. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\services\combat_ready_action_service.py backend\api\combat\ready_actions.py backend\api\combat\schemas.py`, `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ready_attack_endpoint_sets_trusted_ready_state backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ready_action_enters_reach_match_waits_until_target_moves_into_reach -q`, `npm run test -- src\components\combat\__tests__\CombatHudSkillBar.test.jsx`, `npm run test -- src\utils\__tests__\combatSkillActions.test.js`, and `node --check artifacts\enemy-ready-action-ws-smoke.mjs`. Real WS smoke `ENEMY_READY_SMOKE_MODE=enters-reach-trigger BACKEND_ORIGIN=http://127.0.0.1:8002 node artifacts\enemy-ready-action-ws-smoke.mjs` seeded an enemy ready attack with `trigger_match="enters_reach"`, verified the first move `8,6 -> 7,6` produced no ready result and kept the ready action armed, then verified the second move `7,6 -> 6,6` entered 5ft reach, triggered the enemy ready attack, returned `ready_action_results[0].trigger_match="enters_reach"`, hit `65 vs AC12`, dealt 5 slashing damage, changed hero HP `20 -> 15`, consumed the enemy reaction, cleared the ready action, and delivered the result through `entity_moved`; cleanup returned browser/profile/snapshot `0/0/0`, and no `8002`, `3000`, or `3100` listener remained after shutdown. Remaining Ready Action work is a final Ready Action mini-regression before treating the slice as Stage-4-closed.

Ready action 2026-06-08 structured `leaves_reach` real-smoke follow-up: melee Ready Attack now resolves `leaves_reach` at the mover's pre-leave position instead of checking melee range only after the target has already moved out of reach. `prepare_direct_attack` accepts an optional `positions_override`, and Ready Attack builds that override only for non-ranged `trigger_match="leaves_reach"` so ordinary attacks and other ready triggers keep their existing position semantics. Real WS smoke `ENEMY_READY_SMOKE_MODE=leaves-reach-trigger BACKEND_ORIGIN=http://127.0.0.1:8002 node artifacts\enemy-ready-action-ws-smoke.mjs` seeded an enemy ready attack with `trigger_match="leaves_reach"` and isolated the ready-action reaction from automatic opportunity attacks by marking the moving hero as disengaged. Remaining Ready Action work is a final Ready Action mini-regression before treating the slice as Stage-4-closed.

Ready action 2026-06-08 final mini-regression follow-up: Ready Action now takes priority over automatic opportunity attacks for the same reacting actor when both would be caused by the same movement. `matching_ready_action_actor_ids_for_movement` identifies actors whose readied action matches the movement before opportunity resolution, and `resolve_opportunity_attacks(..., excluded_actor_ids=...)` skips those actors in both player-movement and AI-movement paths; this prevents a matching Ready Move/Attack/Spell from degrading into `reaction_already_used` because an automatic opportunity attack consumed the reaction first. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\services\combat_ready_action_service.py backend\services\combat_opportunity_attack_service.py backend\api\combat\movement.py backend\api\combat\ai_turn_attack.py backend\services\combat_direct_attack_service.py backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py`, `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m pytest backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_enemy_ready_attack_triggers_when_player_moves backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_enemy_ready_move_triggers_when_player_moves backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_enemy_ready_spell_cantrip_triggers_when_player_moves backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ready_action_reports_reaction_already_used_when_triggered_by_movement backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ready_action_enters_reach_match_waits_until_target_moves_into_reach backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ready_action_leaves_reach_match_waits_until_target_moves_out_of_reach -q` (`6 passed`, known pytest cache warning), `npm run test -- src\components\combat\__tests__\CombatHudSkillBar.test.jsx` (`15 passed`), `npm run test -- src\utils\__tests__\combatSkillActions.test.js` (`22 passed`), and `node --check artifacts\enemy-ready-action-ws-smoke.mjs`. Ready Action is treated as closed for the current Stage 4 demo-quality scope; enemy leveled ready spells and enemy spell-attack ready variants remain future P2 expansion candidates, not blockers for Stage 4 progression.

### Attacks And Damage

| Status | Priority | Rule Area | Current State | Done Definition |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [x] | P0 | Weapon attacks | Attack roll and damage roll paths exist. | Melee/ranged weapon attacks enforce range, proficiency, ability modifier, cover, and target validity. |
| [x] | P0 | Direct parsed attacks | Natural-language combat action can resolve common attacks. | Local parser handles common move+attack intent before LLM fallback and never fabricates impossible attacks. |
| [x] | P0 | Damage application | HP, healing, resistance, death save interaction exist. | Damage, healing, temp HP, resistance, vulnerability, immunity, and instant death are covered by shared services. |
| [x] | P1 | Critical hits | Weapon base dice already crit; 2026-05-30: weapon-hit rider dice now also double on crit for two-step, direct, and offhand attack paths, covering sneak attack, Divine Fury, Hex/Hunter's Mark/Divine Favor-style sustained riders, and Absorb Elements without doubling flat modifiers. Divine Smite now receives hit crit context from backend turn state and frontend prompt flow, rolling doubled smite dice on crit while preserving normal slot dice. Spell attacks now roll/store d20 hit context in `/spell-roll`, skip damage on misses, and double spell damage dice on crit without doubling flat modifiers or save-based spells. OpenAPI/TS types were regenerated. 2026-06-16 Stage 7 Feather Fall trusted-foundation follow-up: `backend/services/feather_fall_service.py` now provides the backend-only rule foundation for fall-damage reactions. It detects fall hazards/traps from explicit fall flags, fall/drop distance metadata, fall/falling damage types, and pit/drop/cliff text without overmatching generic bludgeoning traps; validates Bard/Sorcerer/Wizard casters that know or prepare Feather Fall / `ĶĘīĶÉĮõ╣ŗńŠĮ`; chooses and spends the lowest available spell slot; optionally marks a supplied reaction state as spent; caps targets at five creatures; and produces damage-prevention metadata that reduces fall damage to 0 while preserving original event details. Covered by `python -m py_compile backend/services/feather_fall_service.py backend/tests/unit/test_feather_fall_service.py` and `python -m pytest backend/tests/unit/test_feather_fall_service.py -q` (`7 passed`). Remaining work is wiring this foundation into actual exploration/hazard trigger prompts, Adventure/WS projection, decline/resume cleanup, and browser-visible fall-damage resolution.

2026-06-16 Stage 7 Feather Fall trap-trigger integration follow-up: exploration trap triggers can now pass a trusted `feather_fall_caster_id` through `StateApplicator` into `apply_trap_trigger_to_target()`. The backend resolves the normal trap save/damage first, then revalidates the named caster's Feather Fall access, spends the lowest available spell slot, marks a supplied reaction state when present, reduces fall damage to 0, records the Feather Fall metadata in `trap_states.last_trigger`, and adds a structured `reaction` dice-display row alongside the trap save/damage rows. Invalid Feather Fall declarations fall back to the ordinary trap result without trusting client-side damage edits. Covered by `python -m py_compile backend/services/feather_fall_service.py backend/services/exploration_rules_service.py backend/services/state_applicator.py backend/tests/unit/test_feather_fall_service.py backend/tests/unit/test_exploration_rules_service.py backend/tests/unit/test_state_applicator_trap_delta.py` and `python -m pytest backend/tests/unit/test_feather_fall_service.py backend/tests/unit/test_exploration_rules_service.py backend/tests/unit/test_state_applicator_trap_delta.py -q` (`52 passed`). Remaining work is the actual player-facing prompt/decline flow, multiplayer viewer projection, and browser-visible Adventure recovery.

### Class And Subclass Features

| Status | Priority | Rule Area | Current State | Done Definition |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [x] | P0 | Fighter basics | Second Wind and Action Surge endpoint support exist; level-17+ Action Surge now has two short-rest uses through `action_surge_remaining` while preserving legacy `action_surge_used` compatibility. | Resources, rest recovery, action economy, and UI buttons are tested. |
| [x] | P0 | Barbarian Rage | Rage resource/damage handling exists. | Rage start/end, bonus damage, resistance, duration, and rest recovery are tested. |
| [x] | P0 | Rogue Sneak Attack | Sneak attack appears in attack resolution. | Advantage/adjacent ally conditions, once per turn, crit doubling, ranged/finesse requirement, and swashbuckler variant are tested. |
| [~] | P1 | Paladin Smite / Lay on Hands | Smite endpoint and healing pool behavior exist partially; Divine Smite now uses a backend-confirmed hit window, derives undead/fiend extra damage from authoritative enemy type data instead of trusting the client flag, exposes that target flag through pending smite, and has frontend prompt/roll flow for the extra +1d8. Lay on Hands now spends an action for healing and has dedicated poison/disease cure class feature paths that cost 5 pool points, clear the matching condition plus duration metadata, return an immediate `target_state`, and are exposed through the combat skill bar when the Paladin is poisoned or diseased. | Divine Smite on hit, upcast, undead/fiend bonus, Lay on Hands pool, disease/poison cure, and UI are tested. |
| [x] | P1 | Monk Ki | Flurry and Stunning Strike already had class-feature paths. Patient Defense now spends 1 ki and a bonus action to set `turn_state.dodging`; Step of the Wind exposes Dash and Disengage as 1-ki bonus-action class-feature paths, reusing `movement_max` and `disengaged` turn-state semantics. Short and long rests restore Ki to the Monk level-derived pool. Martial Arts is exposed through the Monk skill bar as a bonus-action unarmed attack after a completed Attack action, uses the best STR/DEX modifier for hit and damage, scales the Martial Arts die by level, rejects equipped shields, consumes no weapon resources, and preserves bludgeoning damage through damage resolution. | Flurry, Patient Defense, Step of the Wind, Stunning Strike, ki recovery, and martial arts are implemented and tested. |
| [~] | P1 | Druid Wild Shape | Wild shape HP helpers/subclass effects exist. | Form selection, temp HP pool, attacks, AC, movement, damage carryover, concentration, and ending form are complete. |
| [~] | P1 | Warlock pact behavior | Pact slots and some subclass effects exist. | Pact magic slots, invocations, Eldritch Blast scaling, Hex, and short rest recovery are complete. |
| [~] | P2 | Bard Inspiration | Bardic Inspiration grant is trusted in combat, and granted dice can now be explicitly spent on exploration skill checks, combat attack rolls, death saving throws, end-of-turn condition repeat saves, ordinary spell-imposed saving throws, and multiplayer spell saves through a private target-owned reaction prompt. Unused granted dice expire on rest. Lore Bard Cutting Words now works for incoming attack-total reactions, incoming attack damage-roll reduction, and player-initiated grapple/shove/grapple-escape contested ability checks. Future minute-level time expiry and richer ally-protection variants remain follow-up work. | Bardic Inspiration die grant/use/expire, Cutting Words, and UI prompts are implemented. |
| [ ] | P2 | Cleric Channel Divinity | Not trusted. | Channel Divinity resources, Turn Undead, subclass options, and rest recovery work. |
| [ ] | P2 | Sorcerer Metamagic | Not trusted. | Sorcery points, metamagic options, conversion, and spell modification are implemented. |
| [ ] | P2 | Full subclass progression | Subclass effect data exists. | Each supported subclass has feature unlocks, resources, and tests at meaningful levels. |

#### Legendary/Lair Actions Follow-Ups

- 2026-06-03 area-template Legendary Action follow-up: authored area/template metadata such as `area="15 ft cone"` now derives affected `target_ids` from combat positions and party members when no explicit target list is supplied. The Legendary Action prompt carries affected target names, target count, `area_template`, `area_range_ft`, and anchor metadata; the frontend renders `Area 15ft cone` and submits the derived target array through the existing prompt path. Covered by `backend/tests/unit/test_combat_legendary_action_service.py::test_build_legendary_action_prompt_derives_area_targets_from_cone_template`, `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_legendary_action_area_template_prompt_derives_targets_and_resolves`, `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/LegendaryActionPrompt.test.jsx`, and real headless Chrome smoke screenshot `artifacts/browser-legendary-action-area-template-20260603.png`; residual Chrome/profile/snapshot cleanup returned `0/0/0`.
- 2026-06-03 initiative-count Lair Action follow-up: enemies or top-level lair state can provide `lair_actions`; player end-turn now derives `lair_action_prompt` when turn advancement crosses initiative count 20 (losing ties, so 24 -> 20 does not trigger but 20 -> 18 does), while preserving the previous new-round start fallback when all combatants are below 20 or all remaining combatants are above 20. AI turn advancement now also propagates the same `lair_action_prompt` through `/ai-turn` responses and `combat_update` websocket events, so AI auto-drive pauses on the Lair Action window instead of silently stepping past initiative count 20. `/game/combat/{session_id}/lair-action` reuses the Legendary Action save/attack resolver while recording `lair_action_prompted_round` / `lair_action_used_round` for once-per-round protection. Frontend state, turn controls, AI-turn loop, WS handling, API client, flow handlers, and `LegendaryActionPrompt variant="lair"` render/use/skip the window. Covered by `backend/tests/unit/test_combat_legendary_action_service.py::test_build_lair_action_prompt_derives_area_targets_from_radius_template`, `backend/tests/unit/test_combat_legendary_action_service.py::test_should_prompt_lair_action_when_turn_advance_crosses_initiative_count_20`, `backend/tests/unit/test_combat_legendary_action_service.py::test_should_prompt_lair_action_loses_ties_at_initiative_count_20`, `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_lair_action_round_start_prompt_derives_targets_and_resolves_once_per_round`, `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_lair_action_prompt_triggers_when_advancing_past_initiative_count_20`, `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_ai_turn_surfaces_lair_action_prompt_when_advancing_past_initiative_count_20`, `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/LegendaryActionPrompt.test.jsx`, `frontend/src/hooks/__tests__/useCombatTurnControls.test.js`, `frontend/src/hooks/__tests__/useCombatFlowHandlers.test.js`, `frontend/src/hooks/__tests__/useCombatAiTurns.test.js`, `frontend/src/hooks/__tests__/useCombatPageActions.test.js`, and real headless Chrome smoke screenshots `artifacts/browser-lair-action-round-start-20260603.png`, `artifacts/browser-lair-action-initiative-count-20260603.png`, and `artifacts/browser-lair-action-ai-initiative-count-20260603.png`; residual Chrome/profile/snapshot cleanup returned `0/0/0`.
- 2026-06-03 reaction-deferred Lair Action follow-up: AI attacks that hit a player and create an incoming-attack reaction now attach a deferred initiative-count-20 Lair context instead of losing the prompt while reaction priority is preserved. `/game/combat/{session_id}/reaction` consumes that context after Shield/Absorb Elements/Uncanny Dodge/Hellish Rebuke or decline clears the pending attack reaction, returns/broadcasts `lair_action_prompt`, and the frontend reaction hook pauses on the Lair Action window instead of immediately resuming AI auto-drive. Covered by `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_attack_reaction_resolution_surfaces_deferred_lair_action_prompt`, `frontend/src/hooks/__tests__/useCombatSpecialActions.test.js`, and real headless Chrome smoke screenshot `artifacts/browser-lair-action-attack-reaction-20260603.png`; residual Chrome/profile/snapshot cleanup returned `0/0/0`. 2026-06-04 strengthening: the same `attack-reaction` browser smoke now asserts Absorb Elements' HP rollback, slot spend, `fire_resistance` duration, next-melee-hit rider state, and reaction log payload, then the deferred Seismic Pulse prompt/resolution; screenshot `artifacts/browser-absorb-elements-reaction-lair-deferred-20260604.png`. ### Exploration And Campaign Rules

| Status | Priority | Rule Area | Current State | Done Definition |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [x] | P0 | DM style lock | Campaign-start style selection is persisted and injected into prompts. | Style cannot mutate mid-session and affects tone only, not core math. |
| [x] | P0 | AI companion reactions | DM agent separates main narration from companion reactions. | Companions react without crowding out main scene output or changing backend schema. |
| [~] | P0 | Campaign memory/state delta | State applicator and campaign delta services exist. 2026-06-02 follow-up: `state_delta.loot_discoveries` now reveals backend-seeded hidden loot by reward name or loot id, so DM narration can make non-gold/contested rewards appear in the Loot UI without granting them directly or exposing undiscovered module rewards. Covered by `backend/tests/unit/test_state_applicator_campaign_delta.py`, `backend/tests/unit/test_dm_agent_output.py`, and `backend/tests/unit/test_loot_service.py`. | NPC registry, quest log, world flags, party resources, and consequences persist across sessions. |
| [~] | P1 | Rest rules | Rest endpoint restores long/short rest HP, hit dice, spell slots, several class resources, exhaustion reduction, interrupted rests that grant no recovery, and Wizard Arcane Recovery on short rest. 2026-05-29: Adventure rest now uses a two-step confirmation modal with party impact preview for HP, hit dice, spell slots, removable long-rest conditions, death saves, and short-rest hit-dice risk, covered by `frontend/src/utils/__tests__/restPreview.test.js` and `frontend/src/components/adventure/__tests__/RestModal.test.jsx`. Remaining work is duration validation, richer interruption/risk authoring, and expanded class-specific recovery coverage. | Short/long rest restore correct HP, hit dice, spell slots, features, exhaustion, and interrupted rest outcomes. |
| [~] | P1 | Inventory/equipment economy | Buy/sell/transfer/use item services exist, consumables can apply direct effects, Arrows/Bolts purchases update compatible weapon ammunition when possible, combat can consume tracked ammo/thrown weapon copies, and two-handed weapons now conflict with equipped shields. Remaining work is fuller weapon-slot/offhand enforcement, attunement if used, richer item actions, and multiplayer inventory UX. | Item ownership, equipment slots, attunement if used, consumables, gold, ammo, and multiplayer permissions are covered. |
| [~] | P1 | Stealth and perception procedures | Backend helpers exist for passive perception/investigation, best party passive score, 5e-style group stealth, surprise from ambusher Stealth totals vs passive Perception, light/darkvision visibility, noise-adjusted detection DCs, and hidden-state resolution. Remaining work is mostly frontend surfacing, scene authoring inputs, and broader playtest coverage. | Passive perception, group stealth, surprise, hidden condition, light, and noise are rule-backed. |
| [~] | P1 | Traps and investigation | Backend passive discovery exists for hidden traps, secret doors, clues, and mechanisms. Triggered trap resolution rolls saves and damage, attack-roll traps compare configured attack bonuses to target AC, and `state_delta` can apply trigger/attack/disarm/update outcomes while recording scene-level trap state. Remaining work is mostly frontend surfacing and broader playtest coverage. | Detect, disarm, trigger, save/attack, damage, and persistent trap state are represented. |
| [ ] | P2 | Travel and survival | Not systematic. | Pace, navigation, foraging, random encounters, exhaustion, weather, and mounts are implemented. |
| [ ] | P2 | Social systems | Mostly AI/narrative. | Reputation, factions, NPC disposition, persuasion/deception/intimidation consequences persist and affect options. |

- [~] Build encounter templates with terrain, cover, objectives, enemy roles, and environmental hazards. 2026-05-30 first slice: `backend/services/encounter_template_service.py` infers deterministic templates from parsed module scenes and monsters, attaches them to `game_state.location_graph`, preserves template status across refresh, lets combat init prefer an available template at the current location when the DM did not provide `initial_enemies`, and shows an `ENC` count in the Adventure HUD. 2026-05-30 follow-up: the Adventure Map panel now lets the user select mapped locations and preview each selected location's encounter templates, including status, difficulty, XP budget, enemies, enemy roles, terrain/cover, objectives, hazards, reward hints, and tactics. 2026-05-30 follow-up: `POST /game/sessions/{session_id}/encounter-template/select` lets an authorized session user mark an available current-location template as active; combat init now prefers that selected template and clears the active marker once the encounter is triggered. 2026-05-30 privacy follow-up: player-facing map/HUD projections no longer render hidden encounter templates, enemy details, tactics, or reward hints; - [~] Add loot, treasure, shop, item rarity, and consumable economy loops. Existing inventory/shop loops already cover gold, buy/sell, ammo, consumables, equipment, and party transfer. 2026-05-30 first loot slice: `backend/services/loot_service.py` seeds `game_state.loot_pool` from module `key_rewards` and `magic_items`, `GET /game/sessions/{session_id}/loot` exposes the claimable pool, and `POST /game/sessions/{session_id}/loot/claim` grants gold/items to a session character while marking loot claimed to prevent duplicates. Frontend API helpers are available as `gameApi.getLoot` and `gameApi.claimLoot`. 2026-05-30 follow-up: Adventure now has a visible Loot HUD entry and `LootModal` that loads session rewards, separates available/claimed items, claims a reward for the current player, records a system log, and refreshes the session after claim. 2026-05-30 follow-up: loot items without explicit `cost` now receive rarity-based gp value hints, so common/uncommon/rare/etc. rewards surface an economy value in `LootModal` without changing buy/sell settlement rules. 2026-05-30 follow-up: gold loot now supports `claim_mode=split_party`; `LootModal` exposes a Split action for gold rewards, and the backend distributes uneven remainders deterministically across the current party while preserving split allocations in `loot_pool`. 2026-05-30 follow-up: non-gold loot now supports `claim_mode=party_stash` and `claim_mode=roll_party`; the former records a shared party-stash reward without mutating inventory, and the latter rolls d20 for each party member, awards the item to the highest result, and records per-character roll allocations in `loot_pool`. 2026-05-30 follow-up: shop prices now derive from the character's session location context; market/town/shop locations discount buys and improve sell rates, scarce dungeon/wilderness locations mark up buys and lower sell rates, `/characters/shop/inventory?character_id=...` exposes the active pricing context, and buy/sell settlement uses the same backend pricing service. 2026-05-30 follow-up: merchant stock now also depends on the same location profile; scarce dungeon/wilderness shops expose a limited field-stock list and backend buy rejects out-of-stock direct API purchases. 2026-05-30 follow-up: DM input now includes `reward_context` from `loot_pool`, and the rules-layer prompt tells the DM to use `state_delta.gold_changes` for immediate coin while leaving non-gold or contested rewards to the Loot UI / `/loot/claim` claim, split, share, or roll flow. 2026-05-30 privacy follow-up: module-seeded rewards now start hidden, public session and loot endpoints return only discovered/claimed loot, and hidden module rewards cannot be claimed by direct ID. 2026-06-02 discovery follow-up: DM `state_delta.loot_discoveries` now reveals matching hidden rewards by name/id so discovered non-gold or contested loot can enter the Loot UI claim flow without leaking the whole module reward pool. ## Pressure Test Checklist

### Local Preflight

- [ ] Backend starts cleanly on a chosen port.
- [ ] Frontend starts cleanly and points to the backend.
- [ ] Database is either fresh or intentionally seeded.
- [ ] A parsed module exists or load tests seed one without invoking the LLM parser.
- [ ] Model credentials are available for manual AI playthroughs.
- [ ] Browser console is open and cleared before each feature test.
- [ ] Backend terminal/log is cleared before each feature test.

## Suggested Implementation Order

1. P0 recovery and idempotency: duplicate submit, refresh during pending reaction, stale pending state cleanup. First slice complete for pending combat reactions and stale combat turn-token protection on high-frequency combat actions.
2. P0/P1 multiplayer pressure: repeat the 50-user load smoke in CI or before deployment; local manual/browser pressure gaps were closed on 2026-05-31.
3. P1 combat UX: action economy display, current-turn coach, spell-cast plan, unavailable reasons, reaction before/after HP clarity. 2026-06-01 follow-up: reaction prompts now render structured no-reaction HP, post-reaction HP, prevented damage, and downed-risk previews per option; covered by `frontend/src/utils/__tests__/combatReactionPrompt.test.js`, `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/ReactionPrompt.test.jsx`, and `frontend/src/pages/__tests__/Combat.smoke.test.jsx`. 2026-06-01 follow-up: the combat skill bar now surfaces the highest-priority unavailable reason as a visible summary and prioritizes spent action economy over missing-target hints; covered by `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/CombatHudSkillBar.test.jsx`, `frontend/src/utils/__tests__/combat.test.js`, and `frontend/src/pages/__tests__/Combat.smoke.test.jsx`. 2026-06-02 information-architecture follow-up: Combat HUD now adds a compact intent summary above the skill bar, consolidating player-turn status, action economy, selected target HP/AC/hit chance, weapon mode, and top rule/condition chips into one scan area; covered by `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/CombatHudIntentSummary.test.jsx` and `frontend/src/components/combat/__tests__/CombatHud.test.jsx`.
4. Combat renderer milestone: after demo-quality combat UX stabilization, evaluate the 2D-to-3D/2.5D battlefield direction captured in `docs/combat-3d-renderer-milestone.md`; keep backend rules authoritative and prototype a renderer-neutral scene model before any Unity-style rewrite.

## Update Rules

- When a TODO becomes implemented, add the commit or test file in a short note near the row.
- Do not mark a row `[x]` unless there is either automated coverage or a recorded manual playthrough.
- Prefer one focused feature plus tests per commit.
- Keep public API fields stable unless a schema change is deliberate and OpenAPI/types are regenerated.
- Keep AI output advisory for narration/intent; backend remains authoritative for rules and state.

2026-06-05 Confusion mechanics follow-up: `confused` now blocks real reaction usage through the shared backend reaction gate instead of only rendering a UI chip. The same gate covers direct reaction prompts, opportunity attacks, defender interception, and ready-action trigger resolution; ready-action declaration also rejects confused actors because the later trigger would require a reaction. Turn advancement now applies the Confusion d10 table at the start of the next actor's turn for both player-driven and AI-driven turn advancement: roll 1 spends action/bonus control and moves in a random direction up to available movement, rolls 2-6 spend action/bonus and movement, rolls 7-8 resolve an actual automatic random melee attack through shared attack/damage application, and rolls 9-10 leave normal action/movement available while still blocking reactions. The automatic attack can damage the struck creature, including the concentrating caster, and can trigger the normal concentration check path. Confusion end-of-turn WIS saves now resolve before duration ticking, clear `confused` on success, and preserve frontend dice/state logs for both player and AI turn flows; AI turns also preserve an already-started Confusion turn token so forced effects are not duplicated. Frontend action availability now has a dedicated reaction-lock reason, so `confused` disables reaction and ready-action controls without incorrectly disabling ordinary attacks. Targeted backend/frontend tests cover the shared backend reaction gate, deterministic random movement, no-action rolls, normal-action rolls, automatic random melee damage, end-save condition removal, and frontend reaction/end-save log availability. Real browser smoke `AOE_SAVE_COVER_MODE=confusion-turn-rules node artifacts/aoe-save-cover-browser-smoke.mjs` passed with roll 8 automatic melee damage, concentration-check evidence, successful end-of-turn save removal, visible `Ķ¦ŻķÖżÕø░µāæ` log text, and Chrome/profile/snapshot cleanup `0/0/0`.

2026-06-11 Stage 6 AI-control prompt privacy follow-up: monster and lair control prompts are now projected per viewer in multiplayer combat, so `legendary_action_prompt` and `lair_action_prompt` are visible only to the resolved AI combat driver while ordinary room members receive `null` over both HTTP and WS. The backend mirrors the frontend driver policy: online host first, then first online/member fallback; if no driver can be resolved, control prompts stay hidden. `/game/combat/{session_id}/ai-turn`, `/legendary-action`, and `/lair-action` now require the AI combat driver, while `/end-turn` and reaction responses project prompt payloads before returning to non-drivers. In multiplayer, player-character manual condition edits are restricted to that character's owner; enemy, AI companion, and unclaimed-character manual edits require the AI combat driver. This preserves normal rules-driven condition application from attacks/spells while closing the API backdoor where a guest could add/remove statuses on another player or on monsters just by being in the room. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 Divine Smite trusted-hit window follow-up: `/game/combat/{session_id}/smite` now requires a one-use `turn_states[actor_id].pending_smite` window opened by a backend-confirmed weapon hit from either the two-step `/damage-roll` path or the legacy direct `/action` attack path. The endpoint no longer trusts frontend `target_id` / `is_crit` as authority, no longer falls back to `last_attack_*` or the first living enemy, rejects target or crit mismatches, validates slot levels, and clears `pending_smite` after a successful smite so the hit window cannot be reused. Multiplayer combat snapshots now treat `pending_smite` as private turn-state data, matching `pending_attack`, `pending_spell`, and reaction pending payloads, so other players cannot inspect another character's pending smite target or crit state through HTTP refresh or WS combat updates. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\api\combat\smites.py backend\api\combat\_shared.py backend\api\combat\attack_rolls.py backend\api\combat\attacks.py`, `backend/tests/integration/test_combat_endpoints.py::test_paladin_damage_roll_opens_trusted_pending_smite_window`, `test_smite_uses_pending_smite_crit_context_and_consumes_window`, `test_smite_rejects_without_pending_smite_window_and_preserves_state`, `test_smite_rejects_mismatched_pending_smite_payload_without_consuming_slot`, and `backend/tests/integration/test_multiplayer_ws_realtime.py::test_multiplayer_smite_window_is_owner_bound_and_private`. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 campaign helper speaker authority follow-up: Journal generation and checkpoint saving now require the current exploration speaker before they can write shared campaign memory. `generate_journal()` and `save_checkpoint()` call `assert_multiplayer_exploration_speaker()` after membership validation, so a non-speaker cannot trigger expensive shared generation or mutate `game_state.last_journal` / `session.campaign_state`. The Adventure UI now separates sync-only action blocking from shared-state mutation blocking: ordinary action submission, dice continuation, and personal spell preparation still use the existing sync guard, while rest, Journal generation, checkpoint save, and encounter-template selection use a speaker-aware shared mutation guard. Checkpoint and top-bar shared buttons expose disabled states/reasons without disabling personal prepared-spell updates. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 split-party group management authority follow-up: split-party focus and pending-action clearing now distinguish self-service group actions from cross-group table control. Ordinary members may still focus or clear their own group, while cross-group `groups/focus` and `groups/actions/clear` require the room host or current exploration speaker. `clear_group_actions()` also now rejects nonexistent group ids instead of creating empty ghost pending/readiness entries. The Adventure split-party panel and Room lobby status panel mirror this rule by disabling cross-group focus buttons for ordinary members while keeping host/current-speaker controls available. This closes the Stage 6 backdoor where a room member could steal the table camera or erase another group's queued private intent just by knowing the group id. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 started-room character-claim lock follow-up: `POST /game/rooms/{session_id}/claim-character` now locks character binding once a multiplayer room has started. Pre-start behavior is preserved, including switching lobby characters and taking over an AI companion before the adventure begins, but after `multiplayer.game_started` / `current_scene` / active combat is present a room member may only idempotently re-claim their already bound character. This closes the post-start API backdoor where a member who knew an AI companion id or newly created character id could directly switch control, demote their current player character into AI, or promote a table AI into a player-controlled character after the party had already entered exploration/combat ownership rules. The normal Room UI currently has no AI-takeover button, so this slice is a backend boundary hardening pass rather than a new visible control. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 RoomStateUpdated websocket privacy follow-up: the existing `WSManager._event_for_user()` personalization path is now covered by an integration regression using real `ws_endpoint` QueueWebSocket clients and a network-level smoke using real WebSocket connections. This hardens the split-party privacy invariant for `room_state_updated` broadcasts: HTTP room snapshots and WS room snapshots must both redact other groups' `pending_actions_by_group` text per viewer, while preserving each group's own action text. No business-code change was required because `ws_manager.broadcast()` already applies `public_room_info()` for `room_state_updated`, and the initial WS connection path already fetches `get_room_info(..., viewer_user_id=user_id)`. The new regression protects against future refactors that might bypass this viewer-personalized path. 2026-06-11 Stage 6 member-leave vote cleanup follow-up: voluntary `POST /game/rooms/{session_id}/leave` now broadcasts a viewer-personalized `room_state_updated` snapshot to remaining sockets after `member_left`, excluding the leaving user's socket. The snapshot is built through `get_room_info()`, so `ensure_room_votes()` immediately removes stale kick votes involving the departed member instead of relying on a later manual refresh. This closes the lobby lifecycle gap where clients could merge `member_left` and keep showing an obsolete kick vote in `room_votes` until another room refresh happened. 2026-06-12 P2 held-turn/delay first slice: players can now explicitly delay their current combat turn to the end of the current round through `POST /game/combat/{session_id}/delay-turn`. The endpoint reuses the `/end-turn` stale-token guard, multiplayer actor ownership checks, end-of-turn condition/save processing, next-turn state reset, hazard/ready-action expiry handling, AI/lair/legendary prompt projection, and `turn_changed` broadcast path; when the actor is not already last in the round it rewrites `turn_order` so the next remaining combatant acts at the same `current_turn_index`, preserving the round number and moving the delaying actor after the remaining round participants. `TurnChanged` / `frontend/src/types/ws.d.ts` now expose `turn_order_delayed` and `delayed_turn`, `frontend/src/api/client.js` exposes `delayTurn`, `useCombatTurnControls` shares the same refresh/log/AI auto-drive path used by end turn, and `CombatHudControls` adds a disabled-aware delay button in the turn control grid. OpenAPI and generated frontend API types were refreshed with `python backend/scripts/export_openapi.py` and `npm run types:api`. Covered by `.codex-test-artifacts\backend-venv\Scripts\python.exe -m py_compile backend\api\combat\turns.py backend\schemas\ws_events.py backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py`, `backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_delay_turn_moves_current_player_to_round_end`, `backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_delay_turn_rejects_stale_expected_turn_token`, and `backend\tests\integration\test_combat_endpoints.py::test_end_turn_rejects_stale_expected_turn_token` (`3 passed`), plus frontend coverage `npm run test -- src\hooks\__tests__\useCombatTurnControls.test.js src\components\combat\__tests__\CombatHudControls.test.jsx` (`2 files / 24 passed`) and `npm run build`. The new `/game/sessions/{session_id}/exploration-reaction` endpoint accepts `feather_fall` or `decline`, reuses the saved trap resolution without rerolling, validates the prompted reactor, spends the slot on accept, prevents the fall damage, applies ordinary saved damage on decline, clears the pending prompt, records trap state/log dice rows, and resumes multiplayer speaker advancement after resolution. Adventure now restores the prompt, renders a Feather Fall accept/decline panel, submits the decision through the backend, and logs the returned trap/reaction dice rows.
